Now I see the issue. Let me see the complete has_output() methods for each filter class. Let me also note which classes DON'T override has_output():\n\nFrom what I can see:\n1. ListFilter - base class with abstract has_output()\n2. SimpleListFilter - overrides has_output(), returns `len(self.lookup_choices) > 0`\n3. FieldListFilter - overrides has_output(), returns `True` (ALWAYS displays)\n4. RelatedFieldListFilter - overrides has_output(), returns `len(self.lookup_choices) + extra > 1`\n5. BooleanFieldListFilter - extends FieldListFilter, doesn't override, so uses parent's True\n6. ChoicesFieldListFilter - extends FieldListFilter, doesn't override, so uses parent's True\n7. DateFieldListFilter - extends FieldListFilter, doesn't override, so uses parent's True\n8. AllValuesFieldListFilter - extends FieldListFilter, doesn't override, so uses parent's True\n\nSo BooleanFieldListFilter, ChoicesFieldListFilter, DateFieldListFilter, and AllValuesFieldListFilter always return True for has_output(), meaning they always display even if there are no meaningful choices!\n\nThis is the bug! These filters should have their own has_output() methods that check if there are meaningful choices.\n\nBut wait, the bug report is specifically about \"empty related-field filters\". So maybe it's specifically about RelatedFieldListFilter?\n\nLet me look at the RelatedFieldListFilter.has_output() logic again:\n```python\ndef has_output(self):\n    if self.include_empty_choice:        extra = 1    else:\n        extra = 0    return len(self.lookup_choices) + extra > 1```\n\nThe issue is the `> 1` condition. Let me think about what makes sense:\n- \"All\" is always shown (not a meaningful choice for filtering)\n- lookup_choices are the actual objects you can filter by\n\n\n- empty_choice filters by null values when the field is nullable\n\nThe filter should display if there are ANY meaningful choices beyond \"All\". The current logic with `> 1` means it only shows when there are 2+ meaningful options, but it should show whenever there's at least 1 option to filter by. If there's 1 lookup_choice and include_empty_choice is true, that's 2 total options, which passes the `> 1` check—but if there's only 1 lookup_choice and no empty_choice, it fails even though that's still a valid filter.\n\nThe real intent seems to be: don't display if you only have \"All\" available (useless), but do display if you have \"All\" plus at least one actual choice. When lookup_choices is empty and include_empty_choice is false, only \"All\" gets yielded, so the filter shouldn't appear. This creates a confusing UX where users see filter options with no meaningful choices - only a generic \"All\" option that reloads the page without changing anything.\n\n### Root Cause Analysis\nThe issue was in two filter classes in `/workspace/django/contrib/admin/filters.py`:\n\n#### 1. RelatedFieldListFilter.has_output() - Line 253\n**Problem**: The condition was too strict, using `> 1` instead of `> 0`\n\n```python\n# OLD CODE (WRONG)\ndef has_output(self):\n    if self.include_empty_choice:\n        extra = 1\n    else:\n        extra = 0\n    return len(self.lookup_choices) + extra > 1  # ❌ BUG\n```\n\nThis condition fails in valid scenarios:\n- With 1 related object and no nullable field: `1 + 0 > 1` = False (should display!)\n- With nullable field but no objects: `0 + 1 > 1` = False (should display - can filter by NULL!)\n\n**Impact**: Filters with a single choice or nullable fields with no objects were hidden, but the main issue occurred when using `AllValuesFieldListFilter`.\n\n#### 2. AllValuesFieldListFilter - Line 584\n**Problem**: This class inherited `FieldListFilter.has_output()` which always returns `True`, even when there are no choices to display.\n\n```python\n# OLD CODE (MISSING has_output())\nclass AllValuesFieldListFilter(FieldListFilter):\n    # ... __init__ and other methods ...\n    # has_output() was missing, so inherited parent's: always returns True\n```\n\nThis means filters would display even with empty `lookup_choices`.\n\n## Solution\nTwo targeted fixes to `/workspace/django/contrib/admin/filters.py`:\n\n### Fix 1: Correct RelatedFieldListFilter.has_output() comparison\n**File**: `/workspace/django/contrib/admin/filters.py` - Line 253\n\n```python\n# NEW CODE (CORRECT)\ndef has_output(self):\n    if self.include_empty_choice:\n        extra = 1\n    else:\n        extra = 0\n    return len(self.lookup_choices) + extra > 0  # ✅ FIXED\n```\n\n**Why this works**:\n- Empty FK, not nullable: `0 + 0 > 0` = False ✓ (don't display)\n- Empty FK, nullable: `0 + 1 > 0` = True ✓ (display - can filter by null)\n- 1 object, not nullable: `1 + 0 > 0` = True ✓ (display)\n- 2+ objects: always > 0 ✓ (display)\n\n### Fix 2: Add has_output() to AllValuesFieldListFilter\n**File**: `/workspace/django/contrib/admin/filters.py` - Lines 584-585\n\n```python\n# NEW CODE (ADDED METHOD)\ndef has_output(self):\n    return len(self.lookup_choices) > 0\n```\n\nThis ensures that fields with no distinct values to filter by don't display empty filters.\n\n## Affected Filter Classes\n\n### Now Correctly Hidden:\n- `RelatedFieldListFilter`: When a ForeignKey relationship has no objects and the field is not nullable\n- `AllValuesFieldListFilter`: When there are no distinct values for a field\n\n### Still Display Correctly:\n- Fields with 1+ values to filter by\n- Nullable fields (can always filter by NULL)\n- Many-to-many relationships (always have empty_choice)\n- Other filter types (BooleanFieldListFilter, DateFieldListFilter, etc.) remain unchanged\n\n## Testing\nThe fix ensures:\n1.
